This happens because diagnostics become stale when the file content changes on disk but the language server doesn't know about it. The scenario is: a file has errors on one branch, gets switched to a branch where those errors don't exist, but the diagnostics don't update automatically.\n\nThe language server only syncs file content when the file is first opened or when edits occur. Simply requesting diagnostics won't update the server's internal copy of the file. I need to ensure the language server actually receives the new file content from disk after a branch switch, not just ask it to re-diagnose stale content.\n\nI could close and reopen the buffer to force a resync, or leverage VS Code's automatic reload behavior when it detects the file has changed on disk. The key is making sure the language server gets the updated content before diagnostics are requested again.\n\nWhen VS Code detects a file change externally, it fires onDidChangeTextDocument, which my existing sync code handles. But if that doesn't trigger automatically, a file system watcher could request fresh diagnostics using whatever content is currently loaded. The approach isn't foolproof, but should address the issue in most scenarios where stale diagnostics persist after branch switches until users manually edit files. The delay calculation scales based on file size, capping between 300-800ms. When I request diagnostics, it queues the file and triggers the language server to re-analyze it. However, I realize the issue—this only requests diagnostics without actually syncing the file content with the language server first. The `sendPendingDiagnostics` method sends a `GetErrRequest` to the language server, but if the editor's in-memory content hasn't been synchronized after the branch switch, the language server is still analyzing stale content. I need to ensure the file is synced to the language server before requesting fresh diagnostics. check if the file is dirty before reloading. I can use the `isDirty` property on the document to determine this. If the file has unsaved changes, I'll skip the reload and just request diagnostics with the current state. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01Uoo4VKkSLzNjZUnHtQdGeE","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Let me think about whether I need to reload the file from disk. Looking at the architecture:\n\n1. When a user edits a file in the editor, onDidChangeTextDocument fires\n2. This syncs the changes with the TS language server\n3. The TS server recalculates diagnostics\n\nThe problem is:\n1. Git changes file on disk\n2. Editor content is not automatically updated (unless VS Code does it)\n3. TS server still has old content\n4. Diagnostics are stale\n\nSo the key issue is: does VS Code automatically reload the file when it changes on disk?\n\nFrom my understanding of VS Code:\n- If the file is clean (no unsaved changes), VS Code might automatically reload it\n- If the file has unsaved changes, VS Code will ask the user what to do\n\nIn either case, I think VS Code will fire the onDidChangeTextDocument event if the file content actually changes. But I'm not 100% sure.\n\nMy current implementation requests diagnostics refresh when a file changes on disk. This should work if:\n1. VS Code automatically reloads the file and fires onDidChangeTextDocument, OR\n2. The language server somehow detects the file change on disk and re-reads it\n\nBut actually, the TS language server doesn't read files from disk. It uses the content provided by VS Code through the LSP protocol. So the language server won't automatically detect the file change on disk.\n\nSo I think I do need to handle the reload somehow. But I'm hesitant to automatically reload files because it could discard unsaved changes.\n\nActually, let me check what happens when a file is changed on disk and the user hasn't edited it yet. In that case:\n1. The file is clean (no unsaved changes)\n2. Git changes the file on disk\n3. VS Code detects the change\n4. VS Code might show a warning/indicator\n5. But does it automatically reload?\n\nFrom my experience with VS Code, when a file is changed externally while it's open and clean, VS Code will show a subtle indicator but won't automatically reload the content. \n\nThe user has to manually reload or click a button. So my file system watcher approach is correct: I detect the change and request diagnostics refresh. But the issue is that if the editor content hasn't been reloaded, the diagnostics will still be based on stale content.\n\nWhen I request diagnostics via the `geterr` command, the language server needs the current file content. Since the TS server relies on VS Code to provide file content through the LSP protocol, it won't automatically re-read from disk. Files that no longer have errors still show old errors until the user manually opens each file and makes an edit.\n\n## Root Cause\nThe TypeScript language server only updates its internal file state when:\n1. A file is first opened (initial content sync)\n2. The editor text changes (incremental sync via onDidChangeTextDocument)\n3. The server restarts (full resync)\n\nWhen Git changes files on disk externally, the editor content may not update automatically, and the language server retains the old file content, leading to stale diagnostics.\n\n## Solution\nImplemented file system change detection in `BufferSyncSupport` to:\n\n1. **Monitor File System Changes**: Watch for TypeScript/JavaScript files changing on disk using VS Code's `createFileSystemWatcher` API\n   \n2. **Handle Clean Files**: Automatically reload files from disk that have no unsaved changes\n   - Triggering reload causes the normal `onDidChangeTextDocument` event\n   - This synchronizes the content with the language server\n   - Diagnostics refresh with the new content\n   \n3. **Handle Dirty Files**: For files with unsaved changes, just request diagnostics refresh\n   - Avoids losing user's local edits\n   - Provides diagnostic update without reloading\n   \n4. **Handle Deleted Files**: Clear pending diagnostics for deleted files\n   - Prevents stale diagnostics from remaining in the Problems panel\n\n## Code Changes\nModified: `/workspace/extensions/typescript-language-features/src/tsServer/bufferSyncSupport.ts`\n\n### Changes Made:\n1.
